Kihei, Maui, Hawaii” 
Dear Ms. Winchester: 
This report summarizes our earthwork observation and testing services performed 
during the site grading operations and utility installation for the Kihei High School Phase 2 
project from November 2, 2020 to February 7, 2023 in accordance with our fee proposal 
dated August 9, 2018. 
PROJECT CONSIDERATIONS 
The project site encompasses approximately 70 acres of undeveloped land east of 
Piilani Highway, between Kulanihakoi and Waipuilani Gulches, as shown on the Project 
Location Map, Plate 1, and Site Plan, Plate 2. Phase 2 of the project included the 
G70 
Page 2 
W.O. 7480-10(B) 
March 17, 2023 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California  
construction of the new infrastructure and building structures, including the following 
elements described below: 
Site grading, including excavation and embankment throughout the 
campus. 
Preparation of subgrade for the building pads and installation of utilities for 
Buildings A, B, C, D, and H.  
Paving of asphaltic concrete Driveways “A,” “B,” “C,” “E,” and “H,” and 
Aisle “C.” 
Paving of an asphaltic concrete parking lot adjacent to Driveway “C.” 
Concrete pavement installation at Driveway “E.” 
Excavation and backfilling for utility installation. 
Construction of a temporary open field and a basketball court.  
EARTHWORK OPERATIONS 
The site grading and utility installation work for the Kihei High School Phase 2 
project was observed by Geolabs, Inc. from November 2, 2020 to February 7, 2023.  In 
general, Geolabs, Inc. observed mass grading, utility trench backfill and compaction, 
roadway base course placement and compaction, and asphaltic concrete pavement 
placement and compaction. Goodfellow Bros., Inc. performed the site grading and utility 
installation work, and Maui Paving performed the asphaltic concrete paving work.  During 
the site grading and backfilling operations, samples of the on-site and imported materials 
utilized as fill and backfill materials were obtained and transported to our laboratory for 
testing.  The maximum dry densities and optimum moisture contents were established in 
our laboratory in general accordance with ASTM D1557 (Modified Proctor), and the test 
results for materials used in the project are summarized in the attached Appendix A 
(Plate A). The maximum theoretical densities obtained for various asphaltic concrete 
mixes used on the project are summarized in the attached Appendix B (Plate B). 
The fill and backfill materials were moisture-conditioned to above optimum moisture 
content and compacted in accordance with project specifications to a minimum of 90 or 
95 percent of the maximum dry density as determined in accordance with ASTM D1557. 
During the site grading and backfilling operations, periodic field density tests were 
performed in general accordance with ASTM D6938 (Nuclear Gauge Method).  Results of 
the compaction tests performed at the project site are summarized in the attached 
Appendix A (Plates A-1 through A-178). These tests were performed on the prepared 
ground surfaces and on constructed fills and backfills at the site.  Test locations and 
elevations were estimated by pacing and interpolating from on-site survey stakes or 
G70 
Page 3 
W.O. 7480-10(B) 
March 17, 2023 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California  
obtained from the contractor’s grade setter when available.  These locations and 
elevations should be considered accurate only to the degree implied by the methods used.  
Areas assessed as unsatisfactory were reworked until the specified minimum compaction 
was obtained and/or approved by our field representative based on visual observation and 
hand probing. 
During the asphaltic concrete paving operations, periodic field density tests were 
performed in general accordance with ASTM D6938 (Nuclear Gauge Method).  It should 
be noted that Maui Paving performed quality control (QC) testing of the asphaltic concrete 
pavement, and our field tests were performed as spot checks only. Results of the field 
density tests performed at the project site for the asphaltic concrete pavement are 
summarized in the attached Appendix B (Plates B-1 through B-4). These tests were 
performed on the prepared pavement surfaces.  Test locations and elevations were 
estimated by pacing and interpolating from on-site survey stakes.  These locations and 
elevations should be considered accurate only to the degree implied by the methods used.   
Structural fill consisting of material particles no larger than 6 inches in the largest 
dimension and containing between 10 and 30 percent particles passing the No. 200 sieve 
were used at portions of the project.  Since conventional compaction testing is generally 
not practical in these “structural” fills, a testing program to evaluate the number of passes 
by a specific compactor needed to achieve the desired level of compaction was 
performed. Hand probe and visual observations were used during the compaction of the 
“structural” fills to confirm a firm, unyielding compacted material. 
Our services consisted of full-time and part-time field observation of the contractor’s 
fill and backfill placement, subgrade preparation, and compaction procedures during the 
above grading operations. 
Based on the observations of our field representatives and the results of the 
referenced tests, it is our opinion that the site grading and backfill installation work for the 
Kihei High School Phase 2 project, observed and tested by Geolabs, Inc. in the period 
covered by this report, was performed in conformance with the general intent of the 
following references: 
1. 
Project plans and specifications. 
2. 
Report by Geolabs, Inc. entitled, “Geotechnical Engineering Exploration, 
Kihei High School, Phase 1 Infrastructure (On-Site & Off-Site), Kihei, Maui, 
Hawaii”, dated December 8, 2017, and subsequent recommendations; and  
3. 
Report by Geolabs, Inc. entitled, “Geotechnical Engineering Exploration, 
New Building Foundations, Kihei High School, Kihei, Maui, Hawaii”, dated 
March 23, 2018, and subsequent recommendations.

GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California  
LIMITATIONS 
It should be noted that it is not possible to continuously observe all activities 
occurring simultaneously on a construction site. Therefore, some of the earthwork may 
have been performed without our observation. However, the level of earthwork 
observation and testing services provided appears to be reasonable in reducing some 
of the geotechnical risks to the project. It should be recognized that there are variations 
in the accuracy and statistical repeatability of the tests and methods used to monitor 
earthwork construction and materials.  
Our services were performed in accordance with generally accepted standards of 
geotechnical engineering practice; no warranty is expressed or implied. Provision of 
construction monitoring by an engineer is not insurance, nor does it guarantee 
construction of any type. The contractor shall retain responsibility for the quality of the 
work, for adhering to the plans and specifications, and for repairing defects regardless of 
when they are found.
